# AKS EKS GKE and On-Prem Mapping Matrix

Bengali explanation: managed vs self-managed responsibility split বুঝলে architecture decision সহজ হয়।

## Matrix
| Dimension | AKS | EKS | GKE | On-Prem/Self-Managed |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| Networking | Azure CNI or overlay choices | VPC CNI and IP planning | VPC-native model | CNI plugin ownership full |
| IAM Integration | Azure identity integration | IAM role mapping | Workload identity style integration | PKI, RBAC, external IdP wiring |
| Storage | Azure disk or file classes | EBS or EFS style classes | PD and file services | CSI deployment and backend ownership |
| Ingress and LB | Azure LB integration | ELB/ALB ecosystem | Cloud LB integration | Ingress controller and LB infra self-owned |
| Autoscaling | Cluster autoscaler and HPA | ASG or Karpenter patterns | Cluster autoscaler and managed options | Metrics pipeline + autoscaler operations self-owned |
| Upgrade Behavior | Staged control plane and nodepool upgrades | Control plane then node groups | Release-channel influenced upgrades | Full upgrade orchestration via kubeadm and runbooks |
| Responsibility Split | Provider manages control plane | Provider manages control plane | Provider manages control plane | You manage everything |

- learn-kubernetes/02_Kubernetes Overview/008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md::E7 | learn-kubernetes / 02_Kubernetes Overview / 008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.txt | So let's go back in time to the beginning of the container era.
- learn-kubernetes/02_Kubernetes Overview/008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md::E8 | learn-kubernetes / 02_Kubernetes Overview / 008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.txt | And in the beginning there was just Docker and there were other tools like rocket.
- learn-kubernetes/02_Kubernetes Overview/008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md::E9 | learn-kubernetes / 02_Kubernetes Overview / 008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.txt | But Docker's user experience made working with containers super simple, and hence Docker became the most dominant container tool.
- learn-kubernetes/02_Kubernetes Overview/008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md::E10 | learn-kubernetes / 02_Kubernetes Overview / 008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.txt | And then came Kubernetes to orchestrate Docker.
- learn-kubernetes/02_Kubernetes Overview/008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md::E11 | learn-kubernetes / 02_Kubernetes Overview / 008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.txt | So Kubernetes was built to orchestrate Docker specifically in the beginning.
- learn-kubernetes/02_Kubernetes Overview/008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md::E12 | learn-kubernetes / 02_Kubernetes Overview / 008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.txt | So Docker and Kubernetes were tightly coupled and back then Kubernetes only worked with Docker and didn't support any other container solutions.
- learn-kubernetes/02_Kubernetes Overview/008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md::E13 | learn-kubernetes / 02_Kubernetes Overview / 008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.txt | And then Kubernetes grew in popularity as a container orchestrator.
- learn-kubernetes/02_Kubernetes Overview/008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md::E14 | learn-kubernetes / 02_Kubernetes Overview / 008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.txt | And now other container runtimes like rocket wanted in Kubernetes.
- learn-kubernetes/02_Kubernetes Overview/008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md::E15 | learn-kubernetes / 02_Kubernetes Overview / 008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.txt | Users needed it to work with container runtimes that are other than just Docker.
- learn-kubernetes/02_Kubernetes Overview/008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md::E16 | learn-kubernetes / 02_Kubernetes Overview / 008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.txt | And so Kubernetes introduced an interface called Container Runtime Interface or CRE.
- learn-kubernetes/02_Kubernetes Overview/008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md::E17 | learn-kubernetes / 02_Kubernetes Overview / 008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.txt | So CRE allowed any vendor to work as a container runtime for Kubernetes as long as they adhere to the OCI standards.
- learn-kubernetes/02_Kubernetes Overview/008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md::E18 | learn-kubernetes / 02_Kubernetes Overview / 008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.txt | So OCI stands for Open Container Initiative, and it consists of an image spec and a runtime spec.
- learn-kubernetes/02_Kubernetes Overview/008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md::E19 | learn-kubernetes / 02_Kubernetes Overview / 008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.txt | Image spec means the specifications on how an image should be built.
- learn-kubernetes/02_Kubernetes Overview/008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md::E20 | learn-kubernetes / 02_Kubernetes Overview / 008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.txt | So that's what it defined.
- learn-kubernetes/02_Kubernetes Overview/008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md::E21 | learn-kubernetes / 02_Kubernetes Overview / 008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.txt | An image spec defined the specifications on how an image should be built, and the runtime spec defined the standards on how any container runtime should be developed.
- learn-kubernetes/02_Kubernetes Overview/008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md::E22 | learn-kubernetes / 02_Kubernetes Overview / 008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.txt | So keeping these standards in mind, Anyone can build a container runtime that can be used by anybody to work with Kubernetes.
- learn-kubernetes/02_Kubernetes Overview/008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md::E23 | learn-kubernetes / 02_Kubernetes Overview / 008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.txt | So that was the idea.
- learn-kubernetes/02_Kubernetes Overview/008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md::E24 | learn-kubernetes / 02_Kubernetes Overview / 008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.txt | So rocket and other container runtimes that adhere to the OCI standards were now supported as container runtimes for Kubernetes via the CRI.
- learn-kubernetes/02_Kubernetes Overview/008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md::E25 | learn-kubernetes / 02_Kubernetes Overview / 008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.txt | However, Docker wasn't built to support the CRI standards because remember, Docker was built way before CRI was introduced and Docker still was the dominant container tool used by most.
- learn-kubernetes/02_Kubernetes Overview/008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md::E26 | learn-kubernetes / 02_Kubernetes Overview / 008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.txt | Kubernetes had to continue to support Docker as well.
- learn-kubernetes/02_Kubernetes Overview/008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md::E27 | learn-kubernetes / 02_Kubernetes Overview / 008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.txt | And so Kubernetes introduced what is known as Docker shim, which was a hacky but temporary way to continue to support Docker outside of the container runtime interface.
- learn-kubernetes/02_Kubernetes Overview/008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md::E28 | learn-kubernetes / 02_Kubernetes Overview / 008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.txt | While most other container runtimes worked through the CRI, Docker continued to work without it.
- learn-kubernetes/02_Kubernetes Overview/008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md::E29 | learn-kubernetes / 02_Kubernetes Overview / 008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.txt | Now you see Docker isn't just a container runtime alone.
- learn-kubernetes/02_Kubernetes Overview/008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md::E30 | learn-kubernetes / 02_Kubernetes Overview / 008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.txt | Docker consists of multiple tools that are put together, for example, the Docker CLI, the Docker API, the build tools that help in building images.
- learn-kubernetes/02_Kubernetes Overview/008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md::E31 | learn-kubernetes / 02_Kubernetes Overview / 008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.txt | There was support for volumes of security.
- learn-kubernetes/02_Kubernetes Overview/008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md::E32 | learn-kubernetes / 02_Kubernetes Overview / 008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.txt | And finally also the container runtime called Runcie, the daemon that managed Runcie.
- learn-kubernetes/02_Kubernetes Overview/008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md::E33 | learn-kubernetes / 02_Kubernetes Overview / 008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.txt | And that's that was called as container D.
- learn-kubernetes/02_Kubernetes Overview/008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md::E34 | learn-kubernetes / 02_Kubernetes Overview / 008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.txt | So container D is CLI compatible and can work directly with Kubernetes as all other runtimes.
- learn-kubernetes/02_Kubernetes Overview/008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md::E35 | learn-kubernetes / 02_Kubernetes Overview / 008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.txt | So container D can be used as a runtime on its own separate from Docker.
- learn-kubernetes/02_Kubernetes Overview/008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md::E36 | learn-kubernetes / 02_Kubernetes Overview / 008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.txt | So now you have container D as a separate runtime and Docker separately.
- learn-kubernetes/02_Kubernetes Overview/008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md::E37 | learn-kubernetes / 02_Kubernetes Overview / 008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.txt | So Kubernetes continued to maintain support for Docker Engine directly.
- learn-kubernetes/02_Kubernetes Overview/008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md::E38 | learn-kubernetes / 02_Kubernetes Overview / 008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.txt | However, having to maintain the Docker shim was an unnecessary effort and added complications, so it was decided in version 1.24 release of Kubernetes to remove Dockershim completely, and so support for Docker was removed.
- learn-kubernetes/02_Kubernetes Overview/008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md::E39 | learn-kubernetes / 02_Kubernetes Overview / 008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.txt | But you see all the images that were built before Docker was removed.
- learn-kubernetes/02_Kubernetes Overview/008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md::E40 | learn-kubernetes / 02_Kubernetes Overview / 008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.txt | So all the Docker images continue to work because Docker followed the image spec from the OCI standard.
- learn-kubernetes/02_Kubernetes Overview/008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md::E41 | learn-kubernetes / 02_Kubernetes Overview / 008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.txt | So all the images built by Docker follow the standard.
- learn-kubernetes/02_Kubernetes Overview/008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md::E42 | learn-kubernetes / 02_Kubernetes Overview / 008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.txt | So they continue to work with Containerd.
- learn-kubernetes/02_Kubernetes Overview/008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md::E43 | learn-kubernetes / 02_Kubernetes Overview / 008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.txt | But Docker itself was removed as a supported runtime from Kubernetes.
- learn-kubernetes/02_Kubernetes Overview/008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md::E44 | learn-kubernetes / 02_Kubernetes Overview / 008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.txt | So that's the whole story.
